But later in the evening , when Miss Celia be sing like a nightingale , the boy slip away from sleepy Bab and Betty to stand by the syringa bush and listen , with his heart full of new thought and happy feeling ; for never before have he spend a Sunday like this .
And when he go to bed , instead of say `` Now I lay me , '' he repeat the third verse of Miss Celia 's hymn ; for that be his favorite , because his longing for the father whom he have see make it seem sweet and natural now to love and lean , without fear upon the Father whom he have not see .
CHAPTER XII GOOD TIMES Every one be very kind to Ben when his loss be know .
The Squire write to Mr. Smithers that the boy have find friend and would stay where he be .
Mrs. Moss console him in her motherly way , and the little girl do their very best to `` be good to poor Benny . ''
But Miss Celia be his true comforter , and completely win his heart , not only by the friendly word she say and the pleasant thing she do , but by the unspoken sympathy which show itself just at the right minute , in a look , a touch , a smile , more helpful than any amount of condolence .
She call him `` my man , '' and Ben try to be one , bear his trouble so bravely that she respect him , although he be only a little boy , because it promise well for the future .
Then she be so happy herself , it be impossible for those about her to be sad , and Ben soon grow cheerful again in spite of the very tender memory of his father lay quietly away in the safe corner of his heart .
He would have be a very unboyish boy if he have not be happy , for the new place be such a pleasant one , he soon felt a if , for the first time , he really have a home .
No more grubbing now , but daily task which never grow tiresome , they be so varied and so light .
No more cross Pats to try his temper , but the sweet mistress that ever be , since praise be oftener on her lip than blame , and gratitude make willing service a delight .
At first , it seem a if there be go to be trouble between the two boy ; for Thorny be naturally masterful , and illness have leave him weak and nervous , so he be often both domineer and petulant .
Ben have be teach instant obedience to those old than him self , and if Thorny have be a man Ben would have make no complaint ; but it be hard to be `` order round '' by a boy , and an unreasonable one into the bargain .
A word from Miss Celia blow away the threatening cloud , however ; and for her sake her brother promise to try to be patient ; for her sake Ben declare he never would `` get mad '' if Mr . Thorny do fidget ; and both very soon forget all about master and man and live together like two friendly lad , take each other 's ups and down good-naturedly , and find mutual pleasure and profit in the new companionship .
The only point on which they never could agree be legs , and many a hearty laugh do they give Miss Celia by their warm and serious discussion of this vexed question .
Thorny insist that Ben be bowlegged ; Ben resent the epithet , and declare that the leg of all good horseman must have a slight curve , and any one who know any thing about the matter would acknowledge both it necessity and it beauty .
Then Thorny Would observe that it might be all very well in the saddle , but it make a man waddle like a duck when afoot ; whereat Ben would retort that , for his part , he would rather waddle like a duck than tumble about like a horse with the stagger .
He have his opponent there , for poor Thorny do look very like a weak-kneed colt when he try to walk ; but he would never own it , and come down upon Ben with crush allusion to centaurs , or the Greeks and Romans , who be famous both for their horsemanship and fine limb .
Ben could not answer that , except by proudly refer to the chariot-races copy from the ancient , in which he have bear a part , which be more than some folk with long leg could say .
Gentlemen never do that sort of thing , nor do they twit their best friend with their misfortune , Thorny would remark ; cast a pensive glance at his thin hand , long the while to give Ben a good shaking .
This hint would remind the other of his young master 's late suffering and all he owe his dear mistress ; and he usually end the controversy by turn a few lively somersault a a vent for his swell wrath , and come up with his temper all right again .
Or , if Thorny happen to be in the wheeled chair , he would trot him round the garden at a pace which nearly take his breath away , thereby prove that if `` bow-legs '' be not beautiful to some benight being they be `` good to go . ''
Thorny like that , and would drop the subject for the time by politely introduce some more agreeable topic ; so the impending quarrel would end in a laugh over some boyish joke , and the word `` legs '' be avoid by mutual consent till accident bring it up again .
The spirit of rivalry be hide in the best of u , and be a helpful and inspire power if we know how to use it .
Miss Celia know this , and try to make the lads help one another by mean of it , -- not in boastful or ungenerous comparison of each other 's gift , but by interchange them , give and take freely , kindly , and be glad to love what be admirable wherever they find it .
Thorny admire Ben 's strength , activity , and independence ; Ben envy Thorny 's learning , good manner , and comfortable surroundings ; and , when a wise word have set the matter rightly before them , both enjoy the feeling that there be a certain equality between them , since money could not buy health , and practical knowledge be as useful a any that can be find in book .
So they interchange their small experience , accomplishment , and pleasure , and both be the good , as well a the happier , for it ; because in this way only can we truly love our neighbor a ourself , and get the real sweetness out of life .
There be no end to the new and pleasant thing Ben have to do , from keep path and flower-beds neat , feed the pet , and run errand , to wait on Thorny and be right-hand man to Miss Celia .
He have a little room in the old house , newly paper with hunt scene , which he be never tire of admire .
In the closet hang several out-grown suit of Thorny 's , make over for his valet ; and , what Ben value infinitely more , a pair of boot , well black and ready for grand occasion , when he ride abroad , with one old spur , find in the attic , brighten up and merely worn for show , since nothing would have induce him to prick beloved Lita with it .
Many picture , cut from illustrated paper , of race , animal , and bird , be stick round the room , give it rather the air of a circus and menagerie .
This , however , make it only the more home-like to it present owner , who felt exceedingly rich and respectable a he survey his premise ; almost like a retired showman who still fondly remembers past success , though now happy in the more private walk of life .
In one drawer of the quaint little bureau which he use , be keep the relic of his father ; very few and poor , and of no interest to any one but himself , -- only the letter telling of his death , a worn-out watch-chain , and a photograph of Senor Jose Montebello , with his youthful son stand on his head , both airily attire , and both smile with the calmly superior expression which gentleman of their profession usually wear in public .
Ben 's other treasure have be steal with his bundle ; but these he cherish and often look at when he go to bed , wonder what heaven be like , since it be lovely than California , and usually fell asleep with a dreamy impression that it must be something like America when Columbus find it , -- `` a pleasant land , where be gay flower and tall tree , with leaf and fruit such a they have never see before . ''
And through this happy hunting-ground `` father '' be for ever rid on a beautiful white horse with wing , like the one of which Miss Celia have a picture .
Nice time Ben have in his little room poring over his book , for he soon have several of his own ; but his favorite be Hamerton 's `` Animals '' and `` Our Dumb Friends , '' both full of interesting picture and anecdote such a boy love .
Still nice time work about the house , help get thing in order ; and best of all be the daily drive with Miss Celia and Thorny , when weather permit , or solitary ride to town through the heavy rain , for certain letter must go and come , no matter how the element rag .
The neighbor soon get use to the `` antic of that boy , '' but Ben know that he be an object of interest a he career down the main street in a way that make old lady cry out and brought people fly to the window , sure that some one be be run away with .
Lita enjoy the fun as much a he , and apparently do her best to send him heel over head , have rapidly earn to understand the sign he give her by the touch of hand and foot , or the tone of his voice .
These performance cause the boy to regard Ben Brown with intense admiration , the girl with timid awe , all but Bab , who burn to imitate him , and try her best whenever she get a chance , much to the anguish and dismay of poor Jack , for that long-suffering animal be the only steed she be allow to ride .
Fortunately , neither she nor Betty have much time for play just now , a school be about to close for the long vacation , and all the little people be busy finish up , that they might go to play with free mind .
So the `` lilac-parties , '' a they call them , be defer till later , and the lad amuse themselves in their own way , with Miss Celia to suggest and advise .
It take Thorny a long time to arrange his possession , for he could only direct while Ben unpack , wonder and admire a he work , because he have never see so many boyish treasure before .
The little printing-press be his especial delight , and leave every thing else in confusion , Thorny teach him it and plan a newspaper on the spot , with Ben for printer , himself for editor , and `` Sister '' for chief contributor , while Bab should be carrier and Betty office-boy .
Next come a postage-stamp book , and a rainy day be happily spend in paste a new collection where each particular one belong , with copious explanation from Thorny a they go along .
Ben do not feel any great interest in this amusement after one trial of it , but when a book contain pattern of the flag of all nation turn up , he be seize with a desire to copy them all , so that the house could be fitly decorate on gala occasion .
Finding that it amuse her brother , Miss Celia generously open her piece-drawer and rag-bag , and a the mania grow till her resource be exhaust , she buy bit of gay cambric and many-colored paper , and startle the store-keeper by purchase several bottle of mucilage at once .
Bab and Betty be invite to sew the bright strip of star , and prick their little finger assiduously , find this sort of needle-work much more attractive than piece bed-quilts .
Such a snipping and pasting , planning and stitching a go on in the big back room , which be give up to them , and such a noble array of banner and petition a soon decorate it wall , would have cause the dull eye to brighten with amusement , if not with admiration .
Of course , the Stars and Stripes hung high , with the English lion ramp on the royal standard close by ; then follow a regular picture-gallery , for there be the white elephant of Siam , the splendid peacock of Burmah , the double-headed Russian eagle , and black dragon of China , the winged lion of Venice , and the prance pair on the red , white , and blue flag of Holland .
The key and mitre of the Papal States be a hard job , but up they go at last , with the yellow crescent of Turkey on one side and the red full moon of Japan on the other ; the pretty blue and white flag of Greece hung below and the cross of free Switzerland above .
If material have hold out , the flag of all the United States would have follow ; but paste and patience be exhaust , so the busy worker rest awhile before they `` fling their banner to the breeze , '' a the newspaper have it .
A spell of ship-building and rigging follow the flag fit ; for Thorny , feel too old now for such toy , make over his whole fleet to `` the child , '' condescending , however , to superintend a thorough repairing of the same before he dispose of all but the big man-of-war , which continue to ornament his own room , with all sail set and a little red officer perpetually wave his sword on the quarter-deck .
These gift lead to out-of-door water-works , for the brook have to be dam up , that a shallow ocean might be make , where Ben 's piratical `` Red Rover , '' with the black flag , might chase and capture Bab 's smart frigate , `` Queen , '' while the `` Bounding Betsey , '' lade with lumber , safely sail from Kennebunkport to Massachusetts Bay .
Thorny , from his chair , be chief-engineer , and direct his gang of one how to dig the basin , throw up the embankment , and finally let in the water till the mimic ocean be full ; then regulate the little water-gate , lest it should overflow and wreck the pretty squadron or ship , boat , canoe , and raft , which soon ride at anchor there .
Digging and paddle in mud and water prove such a delightful pastime that the boy keep it up , till a series of water-wheels , little mill and cataract make the once quiet brook look a if a manufacturing town be about to spring up where hitherto minnow have play in peace and the retiring frog have chant his serenade unmolested .
Miss Celia like all this , for any thing which would keep Thorny happy out-of-doors in the sweet June weather find favor in her eye , and when the novelty have wear off from home affair , she plan a series of explore expedition which fill their boyish soul with delight .
As none of them know much about the place , it really be quite exciting to start off on a bright morning with a roll of wrap and cushion , lunch , book , and draw material pack into the phaeton , and drive at random about the shady road and lane , pause when and where they like .
Wonderful discovery be make , pretty place be name , plan be draw , and all sort of merry adventure befall the pilgrim .
Each day they camp in a new spot , and while Lita nibble the fresh grass at her ease , Miss Celia sketch under the big umbrella , Thorny read or lounge or sleep on his rubber blanket , and Ben make himself generally useful .
Unloading , fill the artist 's water-bottle , pile the invalid 's cushion , set out the lunch , run to and fro for a Bower or a butterfly , climb a tree to report the view , reading , chat , or frolic with Sancho , -- any sort of duty be in Ben 's line , and he do them all well , for an out-of-door life be natural to him and he like it .
`` Ben , I want an amanuensis , '' say Thorny , drop book and pencil one day after a brief interval of silence , break only by the whisper of the young leaf overhead and the soft babble of the brook close by .
`` A what ? ''
ask Ben , push back his hat with such an air of amazement that Thorny rather loftily inquire : `` Do n't you know what an amanuensis be ? ''
`` Well , no ; not unless it 's some relation to an anaconda .
Should n't think you 'd want one of them , anyway . ''
Thorny roll over with a hoot of derision , and his sister , who sit close by , sketch an old gate , look up to see what be go on .
`` Well , you need n't laugh at a feller .
You do n't know what a wombat be when I ask you , and I do n't roar , '' say Ben , give his hat a slap , a nothing else be handy .
`` The idea of want an anaconda tickle me so , I could n't help it .
I dare say you 'd have get me one if I have ask for it , you be such an oblige chap . ''
`` Of course I would if I could .
Should n't be surprise if you do some day , you want such funny thing , '' answer Ben , appease by the compliment .
`` I 'll try the amanuensis first .
It 's only some one to write for me ; I get so tired do it without a table .
You write well enough , and it will be good for you to know something about botany .
I intend to teach you , Ben , '' say Thorny , a if confer a great favor .
`` It look pretty hard , '' mutter Ben , with a doleful Glance at the book lay open upon a strew of torn leaf and flower .
`` No , it be n't ; it 's regularly jolly ; and you 'd be no end of a help if you only know a little .
Now , suppose I say , ` Bring me a `` ranunculus bulbosus , '' ' how would you know what I want ? ''
demand Thorny , wave his microscope with a learned air .
`` Should n't . ''
`` There be quantity of them all round u ; and I want to analyze one .
See if you ca n't guess . ''
Ben star vaguely from earth to sky , and be about to give it up , when a buttercup fell at his foot , and he catch sight of Miss Celia smile at him from behind her brother , who do not see the flower .
`` S'pose you mean this ?
I do n't call 'em rhinocerus bulburses , so I be n't sure . ''
And , take the hint as quickly a it be give , Ben present the buttercup a if he know all about it .
`` You guess that remarkably well .
Now bring me a ` leontodon taraxacum , ' '' say Thorny , charm with the quickness of his pupil , and glad to display his learning .
Again Ben gaze , but the field be full of early flower ; and , if a long pencil have not point to a dandelion close by , he would have be lose .
`` Here you be , sir , '' he answer with a chuckle and Thorny take his turn at be astonish now .
`` How the dickens do you know that ? ''
`` Try it again , and may be you 'll find out , '' laugh Ben .
Diving hap-hazard into his book , Thorny demand a `` trifolium pratense . ''
The clever pencil point , and Ben bring a red clover , mightily enjoy the joke , and think that their kind of botany be n't bad fun .
`` Look here , no fooling ! ''
and Thorny sit up to investigate the matter , so quickly that his sister have not time to sober down .
`` Ah , I 've catch you !
Not fair to tell , Celia .
Now , Ben , you 've get to learn all about this buttercup , to pay for cheat . ''
`` Werry good , sir ; bring on your rhinoceriouses , '' answer Ben , who could n't help imitate his old friend the clown when he felt particularly jolly .
`` Sit there and write what I tell you , '' order Thorny , with all the severity of a strict schoolmaster .
Perching himself on the mossy stump , Ben obediently flounder through the following analysis , with constant help in the spelling , and much private wonder what would come of it : -- `` Phaenogamous .
Exogenous .
Angiosperm .
Polypetalous .
Stamens , more than ten .
Stamens on the receptacle .
Pistils , more than one and separate .
Leaves without stipule .
Crowfoot family .
Genus ranunculus .
Botanical name , Ranunculus bulbosus . ''
`` Jerusalem !
what a flower !
Pistols and crow ' foot , and Polly put the kettle on , and Angy sperm and all the rest of 'em !
If that 's your botany , I wo n't take any more , thank you , '' say Ben , a he pause a hot and red a if he have be run a race .
`` Yes , you Will ; you 'll learn that all by heart , and then I shall give you a dandelion to do .
You 'll like that , because it mean dent de lion , or lion 's tooth ; and I 'll show them to you through my glass .
You 've no idea how interesting it be , and what heap of pretty thing you 'll see , '' answer Thorny , who have already discover how charm the study be , and have find great satisfaction in it , since he have be forbidden more active pleasure .
`` What 's the good of it , anyway ? ''
ask Ben , who would rather have be set to mow the big field than to the task before him .
`` It tell all about it in my book here , -- ` Gray 's Botany for Young People . '
But I can tell you what use it be to u , '' continue Thorny , cross his leg in the air and prepare to argue the matter , comfortably lie flat on his back .
`` We be a Scientific Exploration Society , and we must keep an account of all the plant , animal , mineral , and so on , a we come across them .
Then , suppose we get lose , and have to hunt for food , how be we to know what be safe and what be n't ?
Come , now , do you know the difference between a toadstool and a mushroom ? ''
`` No , I do n't . ''
`` Then I 'll teach you some day .
There be sweet flag and poisonous flag , and all sort of berry and thing ; and you 'd better look out when you be in the wood , or you 'll touch ivy and dogwood , and have a horrid time , if you do n't know your botany . ''
`` Thorny learn much of his by sad experience ; and you will be wise to take his advice , '' say Miss Celia , recall her brother 's various mishap before the new fancy come on .
`` Did n't I have a time of it , though , when I have to go round for a week with plantain leaf and cream stick all over my face !
Just pick some pretty red dogwood , Ben ; and then I be a regular guy , with a face like a lobster , and my eye swell out of sight .
Come along , and learn right away , and never get into scrape like most fellow . ''
Impressed by this warning , and attract by Thorny 's enthusiasm , Ben cast himself down upon the blanket , and for an hour the two head bob to and fro , from microscope to book , the teacher air his small knowledge , the pupil more and more interested in the new and curious thing he saw or heard , -- though it must be confess that Ben infinitely prefer to watch ant and bug , queer little worm and gauzy-winged fly , rather than `` putter '' over plant with long name .
He do not dare to say so , however ; but , when Thorny ask him if it be n't capital fun , he dodge cleverly by propose to hunt up the flower for his master to study , offer to learn about the dangerous one , but plead want of time to investigate this please science very deeply .
As Thorny have talk himself hoarse , he be very ready to dismiss his class of one to fish the milk-bottle out of the brook ; and recess be prolong till next day .
But both boy find a new pleasure in the pretty pastime they make of it ; for active Ben range the wood and field with a tin box slung over his shoulder , and feeble Thorny have a little room fit up for his own use , where he press flower in newspaper book , dry herb on the wall , have bottle and cup , pan and platter , for his treasure , and make a much litter a he like .
Presently , Ben bring such lively account of the green nook where jacks-in-the-pulpit preach their little sermon ; brook , beside which grow blue violet and lovely fern ; rock , round which dance the columbine like rosy elf , or the tree where bird build , squirrel chatter , and woodchuck burrow , that Thorny be seize with a desire to go and see these beauty for himself .
So Jack be saddle , and go plodding , scramble , and wander into all manner of pleasant place , always bring home a strong , brown rider than he carry away .
This delighted Miss Celia ; and she gladly saw them ramble off together , leave her time to stitch happily at certain dainty bit of sewing , write voluminous letter , or dream over others quite a long , swing in her hammock under the lilac .
CHAPTER XIII SOMEBODY RUNS AWAY '' ` School be do , Now we 'll have fun , '' Sung Bab and Betty , slam down their book a if they never mean to take them up again , when they come home on the last day of June .
Tired teacher have dismiss them for eight whole week , and go away to rest ; the little school-house be shut up , lesson be over , spirit rise fast , and vacation have begin .
The quiet town seem suddenly inundate with child , all in such a rampant state that busy mother wonder how they ever should be able to keep their frisky darling out of mischief ; thrifty father plan how they could bribe the idle hand to pick berry or rake hay ; and the old folk , while wish the young folk well , secretly bless the man who invent school .
The girl immediately begin to talk about picnic , and have them , too ; for little hat spring up in the field like a new sort of mushroom , -- every hillside bloom with gay gown , look a if the flower have go out for a walk ; and the wood be full of featherless bird chirp away as blithely a the thrush , robin , and wren .
The boy take to base-ball like duck to water , and the common be the scene of tremendous battle , wag with much tumult , but little bloodshed .
To the uninitiated , it appear a if these young men have lose their wit ; for , no matter how warm it be , there they be , tear about in the mad manner , jacket off , sleeve roll up , queer cap fling on any way , all bat shabby leather ball , and catch the same , a if their life depend on it .
Every one talk in his gruffest tone , bawl at the top of his voice , squabble over every point of the game , and seem to enjoy himself immensely , in spite of the heat , dust , uproar , and imminent danger of get eye or teeth knock out .
Thorny be an excellent player , but , not be strong enough to show his prowess , he make Ben his proxy ; and , sit on the fence , act a umpire to his heart 's content .
Ben be a promising pupil , and make rapid progress ; for eye , foot , and hand have be so well trained , that they do him good service now ; and Brown be consider a first-rate `` catcher '' .
Sancho distinguish himself by his skill in hunt up stray ball , and guard jacket when not need , with the air of one of the Old Guard on duty at the tomb of Napoleon .
Bab also long to join in the fun , which suit her good than `` stupid picnic '' or `` fussing over doll ; '' but her hero would not have her at any price ; and she be oblige to content herself with sit by Thorny , and watch with breathless interest the vary fortune of `` our side . ''
A grand match be plan for the Fourth of July ; but when the club meet , thing be find to be unpropitious .
Thorny have go out of town with his sister to pass the day , two of the best player do not appear , and the others be somewhat exhaust by the festivity , which begin at sunrise for them .
So they lay about on the grass in the shade of the big elm , languidly discuss their various wrong and disappointment .
`` It 's the mean Fourth I ever saw .
Ca n't have no cracker , because somebody 's horse get scar last year , '' growl Sam Kitteridge , bitterly resent the stern edict which forbid free-born citizen to burn as much gunpowder a they like on that glorious day .
`` Last year Jimmy get his arm blow off when they fire the old cannon .
Did n't we have a lively time go for the doctor and get him home ? ''
ask another boy , look a if he felt defraud of the most interesting part of the anniversary , because no accident have occur .
`` Ai n't go to be firework either , unless somebody 's barn burn up .
Do n't I just wish there would , '' gloomily respond another youth who have so rashly indulge in pyrotechnic on a former occasion that a neighbor 's cow have be roast whole .
`` I would n't give two cent for such a slow old place a this .
Why , last Fourth at this time , I be rumble though Boston street on top of our big car , all in my best toggery .
Hot a pepper , but good fun look in at the upper window and hear the woman scream when the old thing waggle round and I make believe I be go to tumble off , say Ben , lean on his bat with the air of a man who have see the world and felt some natural regret at descend from so lofty a sphere .
`` Catch me cuttin ' away if I have such a chance a that ! ''
answer Sam , try to balance his bat on his chin and get a smart rap across the nose a he fail to perform the feat .
`` Much you know about it , old chap .
It 's hard work , I can tell you , and that would n't suit such a lazy-bones .
Then you be too big to begin , though you might do for a fat boy if Smithers want one , '' say Ben , survey the stout youth , with calm contempt .
`` Let 's go in swimming , not loaf round here , if we ca n't play , '' propose a red and shiny boy , pant for a game of leap-frog in Sandy pond .
`` May as well ; do n't see much else to do , '' sigh Sam , rise like a young elephant .
The others be about to follow , when a shrill `` Hi , hi , boy , hold on ! ''
make them turn about to behold Billy Barton tear down the street like a runaway colt , wave a long strip of paper a he run .
`` Now , then , what 's the matter ? ''
demand Ben , a the other come up grinning and puffing , but full of great news .
`` Look here , read it !
I 'm go ; come along , the whole of you , '' pant Billy , put the paper into Sam 's hand , and survey the crowd with a face as beaming a a full moon .
`` Look out for the big show , '' read Sam .
`` Van Amburgh & Co. 's New Great Golden Menagerie , Circus and Colosseum , will exhibit at Berryville , July 4th , at 1 and 7 precisely .
Admission 50 cent , child half-price .
Do n't forget day and date .
H. Frost , Manager . ''
While Sam read , the other boy have be gloat over the enticing picture which cover the bill .
There be the golden car , fill with noble being in helmet , all play on immense trumpet ; the twenty-four prancing steed with mane , tail , and feather head toss in the breeze ; the clown , the tumbler , the strong men , and the rider fly about in the air a if the law of gravitation no longer exist .
But , best of all , be the grand conglomeration of animal where the giraffe appear to stand on the elephant 's back , the zebra to be jump over the seal , the hippopotamus to be lunch off a couple of crocodile , and lion and tiger to be rain down in all direction with their mouth , wide open and their tail as stiff a that of the famous Northumberland House lion .
`` Cricky !
would n't I like to see that , '' say little Cyrus Fay , devoutly hop that the cage , in which this pleasing spectacle take place , be a very strong one .
`` You never would , it 's only a picture !
That , now , be something like , '' and Ben , who have prick up his ear at the word `` circus , '' lay his finger on a small cut of a man hanging by the back of his neck with a child in each hand , two men suspend from his foot , and the third swing forward to alight on his head .
`` I 'm go , '' say Sam , with calm decision , for this superb array of unknown pleasure fire his soul and make him forget his weight .
`` How will you fix it ? ''
ask Ben , finger the bill with a nervous thrill all through his wiry limb , just a he use to feel it when his father catch him up to dash into the ring .
`` Foot it with Billy .
It 's only four mile , and we 've get lot of time , so we can take it easy .
Mother wo n't care , if I send word by Cy , '' answer Sam , produce half a dollar , a if such magnificent sum be no stranger to his pocket .
`` Come on , Brown ; you 'll be a first-rate fellow to show u round , a you know all the dodge , '' say Billy , anxious to get his money 's worth .
`` Well , I do n't know , '' begin Ben , long to go , but afraid Mrs. Moss would say `` No ! ''
if he ask leave .
`` He 's afraid , '' sneer the red-faced boy , who felt bitterly toward all mankind at that instant , because he know there be no hope of his go .
`` Say that again , and I 'll knock your head off , '' and Ben face round with a gesture which cause the other to skip out of reach precipitately .
`` Has n't get any money , more likely , '' observe a shabby youth , whose pocket never have any thing in them but a pair of dirty hand .
Ben calmly produce a dollar bill and wave it defiantly before this doubter , observe with dignity : `` I 've get money enough to treat the whole crowd , if I choose to , which I do n't . ''
`` Then come along and have a jolly time with Sam and me .
We can buy some dinner and get a ride home , as like a not , '' say the amiable Billy , with a slap on the shoulder , and a cordial grin which make it impossible for Ben to resist .
`` What be you stop for ? ''
demand Sam , ready to be off , that they might `` take it easy . ''

He 'll get lose or steal if I take him , and it 's too far to carry him home if you be in a hurry , '' begin Ben , persuade himself that this be the true reason of his delay .

He 'll do it for a cent ; wo n't you , Cy ? ''

`` No , I wo n't ; I do n't like him .
He wink at me , and growl when I touch him , '' mutter naughty Cy , remember how much reason poor Sanch have to distrust his tormentor .

Come here , sissy ; Ben want you , '' call Sam , beckon to a small figure just perch on the fence .

Miss Celia say I Might do what I please , all day .
You remember , now . ''

It be a mistake on Ben 's part , for while his eye be on his work Bab 's be devour the bill which Sam still hold , and her suspicion be arouse by the boy ' face .
`` Where be you go ?
Ma will want to know , '' she say , as curious a a magpie all at once .
`` Never you mind ; girl ca n't know every thing .
You just catch hold of this and run along home .
Lock Sanch up for an hour , and tell your mother I 'm all right , '' answer Ben , bound to assert his manly supremacy before his mate .

`` Circus !
Oh , Ben , do take me ! ''

`` Yes , I could , as easy a not . ''

Miss Celia would n't care , and I 'm go , any way . ''

I 'll be just as good a ever be , and I 'll take care of Sanch all the way , '' plead Bab , clasp her hand and look round for some sign of relent in the face of the boy .

I 'd like to see her walk eight mile .

Girls be such a bother when you want to knock round .
No , Bab , you ca n't go .
Travel right home and do n't make a fuss .

Ben speak very decidedly ; and , take Billy 's arm , away they go , leave poor Bab and Sanch to watch them out of sight , one sobbing , the other whine dismally .
Somehow those two figure seem to go before Ben all along the pleasant road , and half spoil his fun ; for though he laugh and talk , cut cane , and seem as merry a a grig , he could not help feeling that he ought to have ask leave to go , and be kind to Bab .
`` Perhaps Mrs. Moss would have plan somehow so we could all go , if I 'd tell her , I 'd like to show her round , and she 's be real good to me .
No use now .
I 'll take the girl a lot of candy and make it all right . ''
He try to settle it in that way and trudge gayly off , hop Sancho would n't feel hurt at be leave , wonder if any of `` Smithers 's lot '' would be round , and plan to do the honor handsomely to the boy .
It be very warm ; and just outside of the town they pause by a wayside watering-trough to wash their dusty face , and cool off before plunge into the excitement of the afternoon .
As they stand refresh themselves , a baker 's cart come jingling by ; and Sam propose a hasty lunch while they rest .
A supply of gingerbread be soon buy ; and , climb the green bank above , they lay on the grass under a wild cherry-tree , munch luxuriously , while they feast their eye at the same time on the splendor await them ; for the great tent , with all it flag fly , be visible from the hill .
`` We 'll cut across those field , -- it 's short than go by the road , -- and then we can look round outside till it 's time to go in .
I want to have a good go at every thing , especially the lion , '' say Sam , begin on his last cookie .
`` I hear 'em roar just now ; '' and Billy stand up to gaze with big eye at the flap canvas which hide the king of beast from his long sight .
`` That be a cow mooing .

CHAPTER XVIII BOWS AND ARROWS If Sancho 's abduction make a stir , one may easily imagine with what warmth and interest he be welcome back when his wrong and wandering be know .

`` A century or more ago , in a small settlement on the bank of the Connecticut , -- which mean the Long River of Pines , -- there live a little girl call Matty Kilburn .
On a hill stand the fort where the people run for protection in any danger , for the country be new and wild , and more than once the Indians have come down the river in their canoe and burn the house , kill men , and carry away woman and child .
Matty live alone with her father , but felt quite safe in the log house , for he be never far away .
One afternoon , a the farmer be all busy in their field , the bell rang suddenly , -- a sign that there be danger near , -- and , drop their rake or ax , the men hurry to their house to save wife and baby , and such few treasure a they could .
Mr. Kilburn catch up his gun with one hand and his little girl with the other , and run as fast a he could toward the fort .
But before he could reach it he hear a yell , and saw the red men come up from the river .
Then he know it would be in vain to try to get in , so he look about for a safe place to hide Matty till he could come for her .
He be a brave man , and could fight , so he have no thought of hide while his neighbor need help ; but the dear little daughter must be care for first .
`` In the corner of the lonely pasture which they dare not cross , stand a big hollow elm , and there the farmer hastily hide Matty , drop her down into the dim nook , round the mouth of which young shoot have grow , so that no one would have suspect any hole be there .

`` Mr. Kilburn go away , and be take prisoner in the fight , carry off , and for year no one know whether he be alive or dead .

`` But he do n't , '' chirp the robin , fly away , with a contemptuous flirt of his rusty-black tail .
`` That be exactly what you must promise not to do , boys .
Fire away at your target as much a you like , but do not harm any living creature , '' say Miss Celia , a Ben follow arm and equip with her own long-unused accoutrement .
`` Of course we wo n't if you say so ; but , with a little practice , I could bring down a bird as well a that fellow you read to me about with his woodpecker and lark and heron , '' answer Thorny , who have much enjoy the article , while his sister lament over the destruction of the innocent bird .
`` You 'd do well to borrow the Squire 's old stuffed owl for a target ; there would be some chance of your hit him , he be so big , '' say his sister , who always make fun of the boy when he begin to brag .
Thorny 's only reply be to send his arrow straight up so far out of sight that it be a long while come down again to stick quiver in the ground near by , whence Sancho bring it in his mouth , evidently highly approve of a game in which he could join .
`` Not bad for a beginning .
Now , Ben , fire away . ''
But Ben 's experience with bow be small , and , in spite of his praiseworthy effort to imitate his great exemplar , the arrow only turn a feeble sort of somersault and descend perilously near Bab 's uplifted nose .
`` If you endanger other people 's life and liberty in your pursuit of happiness , I shall have to confiscate your arm , boy .
Take the orchard for your archery ground ; that be safe , and we can see you a we sit here .
I wish I have two hand , so that I could paint you a fine , gay target ; '' and Miss Celia look regretfully at the injured arm , which a yet be of little use .
`` I wish you could shoot , too ; you use to beat all the girl , and I be proud of you , '' answer Thorny , with the air of a fond elder brother ; though , at the time he allude to , he be about twelve , and hardly up to his sister 's shoulder .
`` Thank you .
I shall be happy to give my place to Bab and Betty if you will make them some bow and arrow ; they could not use those long one . ''
The young gentleman do not take the hint as quickly a Miss Celia hop they would ; in fact , both look rather blank at the suggestion , a boy generally do when it be propose that girl -- especially small one -- shall join in any game they be play .
`` P ` r ` aps it would be too much trouble , '' begin Betty , in her winning little voice .
`` I can make my own , '' declare Bab , with an independent toss of the head .
`` Not a bit ; I 'll make you the jolly small bow that ever be , Belinda , '' Thorny hasten to say , soften by the appeal glance of the little maid .
`` You can use mine , Bab ; you 've get such a strong fist , I guess you could pull it , '' add Ben , remember that it would not be amiss to have a comrade who shoot bad than he do , for he felt very inferior to Thorny in many way , and , be use to praise , have miss it very much since he retire to private life .
`` I will be umpire , and brighten up the silver arrow I sometimes pin my hair with , for a prize , unless we can find something well , '' propose Miss Celia , glad to see that question settle , and every prospect of the new play be a pleasant amusement for the hot weather .
It be astonish how soon archery become the fashion in that town , for the boy discuss it enthusiastically all that even , form the `` William Tell Club '' next day , with Bab and Betty a honorary member , and , before the week be out , nearly every lad be see , like young Norval , `` With bend bow and quiver full of arrow , '' shoot away , with a charm disregard of the safety of their fellow citizen .
Banished by the authority to secluded spot , the member of the club set up their target and practise indefatigably , especially Ben , who soon discover that his early gymnastics have give him a sinewy arm and a true eye ; and , take Sanch into partnership a picker-up , he get more shot out of an hour than those who have to run to and fro .
Thorny easily recover much of his former skill , but his strength have not fully return , and he soon grow tire .
Bab , on the contrary , throw herself into the contest heart and soul , and tug away at the new bow Miss Celia give her , for Ben 's be too heavy .
No other girl be admit , so the outsider get up a club of their own , and call it `` The Victoria , '' the name be suggest by the magazine article , which go the round a a general guide and reference book .
Bab and Betty belong to this club and duly report the doings of the boy , with whom they have a right to shoot if they choose , but soon waive the right , plainly see that their absence would be regard in the light of a favor .
The archery fever rag as fiercely a the base-ball epidemic have do before it , and not only do the magazine circulate freely , but Miss Edgeworth 's story , which be eagerly read , and so much admire that the girl at once mount green ribbon , and the boy keep yard of whip-cord in their pocket like the provident Benjamin of the tale .
Every one enjoy the new play very much , and something grow out of it which be a lasting pleasure to many , long after the bow and arrow be forget .
Seeing how glad the child be to get a new story , Miss Celia be move to send a box of book -- old and new -- to the town library , which be but scantily supply , a country library be apt to be .
This donation produce a good effect ; for other people hunt up all the volume they could spare for the same purpose , and the dusty shelf in the little room behind the post-office fill up amazingly .
Coming in vacation time they be hail with delight , and ancient book of travel , as well a modern tale , be feast upon by happy young folk , with plenty of time to enjoy them in peace .
The success of her first attempt at be a public benefactor please Miss Celia very much , and suggest other way in which she might serve the quiet town , where she seem to feel that work be wait for her to do .
She say little to any one but the friend over the sea , yet various plan be make then that blossom beautifully by-and-by .
CHAPTER XIX SPEAKING PIECES The first of September come all too soon , and school begin .
Among the boy and girl who go troop up to the `` East Corner knowledge-box , '' a they call it , be our friend Ben , with a pile of neat book under his arm .
He felt very strange , and decidedly shy ; but put on a bold face , and let nobody guess that , though nearly thirteen , he have never be to school before .
Miss Celia have tell his story to Teacher , and she , be a kind little woman , with young brother of her own , make thing a easy for him a she could .
In reading and write he do very well , and proudly take his place among lad of his own age ; but when it come to arithmetic and geography , he have to go down a long way , and begin almost at the beginning , in spite of Thorny 's effort to `` tool him along fast . ''
It mortify him sadly , but there be no help for it ; and in some of the class he have dear little Betty to console with him when he fail , and smile contentedly when he get above her , a he soon begin to do , -- for she be not a quick child , and plod through First Parts long after sister Bab be flourish away among girl much old than herself .
Fortunately , Ben be a short boy and a clever one , so he do not look out of place among the ten and eleven year olders , and fell upon his lesson with the same resolution with which he use to take a new leap , or practise patiently till he could touch his heel with his head .
That sort of exercise have give him a strong , elastic little body ; this kind be to train his mind , and make it faculty a useful , quick and sure , a the obedient muscle , nerve and eye , which keep him safe where others would have break their neck .
He know this , and find much consolation in the fact that , though mental arithmetic be a hopeless task , he could turn a dozen somersault , and come up as steady a a judge .
When the boy laugh at him for say that China be in Africa , he rout them entirely by his superior knowledge of the animal belong to that wild country ; and when `` First class in read '' be call , he march up with the proud consciousness that the short boy in it do good than tall Moses Towne or fat Sam Kitteridge .
Teacher praise him all she honestly could , and correct his many blunder so quietly that he soon cease to be a deep , distressful red during recitation , and tug away so manfully that no one could help respect him for his effort , and try to make light of his failure .
So the first hard week go by , and though the boy 's heart have sink many a time at the prospect of a protracted wrestle with his own ignorance , he make up his mind to win , and go at it again on the Monday with fresh zeal , all the good and braver for a good , cheery talk with Miss Celia in the Sunday evening twilight .
He do not tell her one of his great trial , however , because he think she could not help him there .
Some of the child rather look down upon him , call him `` tramp '' and `` beggar , '' twit him with have be a circus boy , and live in a tent like a gypsy .
They do not mean to be cruel , but do it for the sake of teasing , never stop to think how much such sport can make a fellow-creature suffer .
Being a plucky fellow , Ben pretend not to mind ; but he do feel it keenly , because he want to start afresh , and be like other boy .
He be not ashamed of the old life ; but , find those around him disapprove of it , he be glad to let it be forget , even by himself ; for his late recollection be not happy one , and present comfort make past hardship seem hard than before .
He say nothing of this to Miss Celia ; but she find it out , and like him all the good for keep some of his small worry to himself .
Bab and Betty come over Monday afternoon full of indignation at some boyish insult Sam have put upon Ben ; and , find them too full of it to enjoy the reading , Miss Celia ask what the matter be .
Then both little girl burst out in a rapid succession of broken exclamation , which do not give a very clear idea of the difficulty , -- `` Sam do n't like it because Ben jump farther than he do -- '' `` And he say Ben ought to be in the poor-house . ''
`` And Ben say he ought to be in it pigpen . ''

-- such a greedy thing , bring lovely big apple , and not give any one a single bite ! ''

CHAPTER XX BEN 'S BIRTHDAY A superb display of flag flap gayly in the breeze on the September morning when Ben proudly enter his teen .
An irruption of bunting seem to have break out all over the old house , for banner of every shape and size , color and design , fly from chimney-top to gable , porch and gate-way , make the quiet place look as lively a a circus tent , which be just what Ben most desired and delighted in .
The boy have be up very early to prepare the show , and when it be ready enjoy it hugely , for the fresh wind make the pennon cut strange caper .
The winged lion of Venice look a if try to fly away home ; the Chinese dragon appear to brandish his forked tail a he claw at the Burmese peacock ; the double-headed eagle of Russia peck at the Turkish crescent with one beak , while the other seem to be scream to the English royal beast , `` Come on and lend a paw . ''
In the hurry of hoist the Siamese elephant get turned upside down , and now danced gayly on his head , with the star and stripe wave proudly over him .
A green flag with a yellow harp and sprig of shamrock hung in sight of the kitchen window , and Katy , the cook , get breakfast to the tune of `` St. Patrick 's day in the morning . ''

The little girl come out to see , and declare it be the lovely sight they ever behold , while Thorny play `` Hail Columbia '' on his fife , and Ben , mount the gate-post , crow long and loud like a happy cockerel who have just reach his majority .

But he do not forget to thank Mrs. Moss for the cake she send him , nor the girl for the red mitten which they have secretly and painfully knit .

They be very busy all the morning preparing for the festivity to come , and as soon a dinner be over every one scramble into his or her best clothes as fast a possible , because , although invite to come at two , impatient boy and girl be see hover about the avenue as early a one .
The first to arrive , however , be an uninvited guest , for just a Bab and Betty sit down on the porch step , in their stiff pink calico frock and white ruffled apron , to repose a moment before the party come in , a rustling be hear among the lilac , and out step Alfred Tennyson Barlow , look like a small Robin Hood , in a green blouse with a silver buckle on his broad belt , a feather in his little cap and a bow in his hand .

I hear about it .

I like them . ''

CHAPTER XXI CUPID 'S LAST APPEARANCE A picnic supper on the grass follow the game , and then , a twilight begin to fall , the young people be marshal to the coach-house , now transform into a rustic theatre .

Ah sin lo , Pan to fo , Tsing up chin leute ! ''

And when one read the following very inadequate description of the somewhat mixed entertainment , it be impossible to deny that the promise make be nobly keep .

CHAPTER XXII A BOY 'S BARGAIN It be some day before the child be tire of talk over Ben 's birthday party ; for it be a great event in their small world ; but , gradually , new pleasure come to occupy their mind , and they begin to plan the nutting frolic which always follow the early frost .
While wait for Jack to open the chestnut burr , they vary the monotony of school life by a lively scrimmage long know a `` the wood-pile fight . ''
The girl like to play in the half-empty shed , and the boy , merely for the fun of teasing , declare that they should not , so block up the doorway a fast a the girl clear it .
Seeing that the squabble be a merry one , and the exercise well for all than lounge in the sun or reading in school during recess , Teacher do not interfere , and the barrier rise and fell almost as regularly a the tide .
It would be difficult to say which side work the harder ; for the boy go before school begin to build up the barricade , and the girl stay after lesson be over to pull down the last one make in afternoon recess .
They have their play-time first ; and , while the boy wait inside , they hear the shout of the girl , the banging of the wood , and the final crash , a the well-packed pile go down .
Then , a the lassie come in , rosy , breathless , and triumphant , the lad rush out to man the breach , and labor gallantly till all be as tight a hard blow could make it .
So the battle rag , and bruise knuckle , splinter in finger , torn clothes , and rub shoe , be the only wound receive , while a great deal of fun be have out of the maltreated log , and a lasting peace secure between two of the boy .
When the party be safely over , Sam begin to fall into his old way of torment Ben by call names , a it cost no exertion to invent try speech , and slyly utter them when most likely to annoy .
Ben bore it as well a he could ; but fortune favor him at last , a it usually do the patient , and he be able to make his own term with his tormentor .
When the girl demolish the wood-pile , they perform a jubilee chorus on comb , and tin kettle , play like tambourine ; the boy celebrate their victory with shrill whistle , and a drum accompaniment with fist on the shed wall .
Billy bring his drum , and this be such an addition that Sam hunt up an old one of his little brother 's , in order that he might join the drum corp .
He have no stick , however , and , cast about in his mind for a good substitute for the genuine thing , bethink him of bulrush .
`` Those will do first-rate , and there be lot in the ma ` sh , if I can only get 'em , '' he say to himself , and turn off from the road on his way home to get a supply .
Now , this marsh be a treacherous spot , and the tragic story be tell of a cow who get in there and sink till nothing be visible but a pair of horn above the mud , which suffocate the unwary beast .
For this reason it be call `` Cowslip Marsh , '' the wag say , though it be generally believe to be so name for the yellow flower which grow there in great profusion in the spring .
Sam have see Ben hop nimbly from one tuft of grass to another when he go to gather cowslip for Betty , and the stout boy think he could do the same .
Two or three heavy jump land him , not among the bulrush , a he have hop , but in a pool of muddy water , where he sink up to his middle with alarm rapidity .
Much scar , he try to wade out , but could only flounder to a tussock of grass , and cling there , while he endeavor to kick his legs free .
He get them out , but struggle in vain to coil them up or to hoist his heavy body upon the very small island in this sea of mud .
Down they splash again ; and Sam give a dismal groan a he think of the leech and water-snakes which might be lie in wait below .
Visions of the lose cow also flash across his agitated mind , and he give a despairing shout very like a distract `` Moo ! ''
Few people pass along the lane , and the sun be set , so the prospect of a night in the marsh nerve Sam to make a frantic plunge toward the bulrush island , which be near than the mainland , and look firm than any tussock round him .
But he fail to reach this haven of rest , and be force to stop at an old stump which stick up , look very like the moss-grown horn of the `` dear depart . ''
Roosting here , Sam begin to shout for aid in every key possible to the human voice .
Such hoot and howl , whistle and roar , never wake the echo of the lonely marsh before , or scar the portly frog who reside there in calm seclusion .
He hardly expect any reply but the astonished `` Caw ! ''
of the crow , who sit upon a fence watch him with gloomy interest ; and when a cheerful `` Hullo , there ! ''
sound from the lane , he be so grateful that tear of joy roll down his fat cheek .
`` Come on !
I 'm in the ma ` sh .
Lend a hand and get me out ! ''
bawl Sam , anxiously wait for his deliverer to appear , for he could only see a hat bobbing along behind the hazel-bushes that fringe the lane .
Steps crash through the bush , and then over the wall come an active figure , at the sight of which Sam be almost ready to dive out of sight , for , of all possible boy , who should it be but Ben , the last person in the world whom he would like to have see him in his present pitiful plight .
`` Is it you , Sam ?
Well , you be in a nice fix ! ''
and Ben 's eye begin to twinkle with mischievous merriment , as well they might , for Sam certainly be a spectacle to convulse the sober person .
Perched unsteadily on the gnarled stump , with his muddy leg draw up , his dismal face splash with mud , and the whole low half of his body as black a if he have be dip in an inkstand , he present such a comically doleful object that Ben dance about , laugh like a naughty will-o ' - the-wisp who , have lead a traveller astray then fell to jeer at him .
`` Stop that , or I 'll knock your head off ! ''

`` Come on and do it ; I give you leave , '' answer Ben , spar away derisively a the other totter on his perch , and be force to hold tight l he should tumble off .
`` Do n't laugh , there 's a good chap , but fish me out somehow , or I shall get my death sit here all wet and cold , '' whine Sam , change his tune , and feel bitterly that Ben have the upper hand now .
Ben felt it also ; and , though a very good-natured boy , could not resist the temptation to enjoy this advantage for a moment at least .
`` I wo n't laugh if I can help it ; only you do look so like a fat , speckle frog , I may not be able to hold in .
I 'll pull you out pretty soon ; but first I 'm go to talk to you , Sam , '' say Ben , sober down a he take a seat on the little point of land near the stranded Samuel .
`` Hurry up , then ; I 'm as stiff a a board now , and it 's no fun sit here on this knotty old thing , '' growl Sam , with a discontented squirm .

Look here , I 've get you in a tight place , and I do n't mean to help you a bit till you promise to let me alone .
Now then ! ''
and Ben 's face grow stern with his remembered wrong a he grimly eye his discomfited foe .

`` I shall do a I like about that . ''
`` Then I wo n't promise a thing !
I 'm not go to have the whole school laughing at me , '' protest Sam , who hat to be ridicule even more than Ben do .

and Ben walk off with his hand in his pocket as coolly a if the bog be Sam 's favorite retreat .
`` Hold on , do n't be in such a hurry ! ''

`` All right ! ''

Is that what you want ? ''
`` Now I come to think of it , there be one thing more .
I like to make a good bargain when I begin , '' say Ben , with a shrewd air .
`` You must promise to keep Mose quiet , too .
He follow your lead , and if you tell him to stop it he will .

I ai n't , so we 'll try this way . ''
`` Yes , Yes , I 'll see to Mose .

`` Do n't neither !

I will !
-- I will ! ''

`` I never think of that way , '' say Sam , watch him with much inward chagrin at his own failure .
`` I should think you 'd write ` Look before you leap , ' in your copy-book often enough to get the idea into your stupid head .
Come , crook , '' command Ben , lean forward with extend little finger .
Sam obediently perform the ceremony , and then Ben sit astride one of the horn of the stump while the muddy Crusoe go slowly across the rail from point to point till he land safely on the shore , when he turn about and ask with an ungrateful jeer , -- `` Now what 's go to become of you , old Look-before-you-leap ? ''
`` Mud turtle can only sit on a stump and bawl till they be take off , but frog have legs worth something , and be not afraid of a little water , '' answer Ben , hop away in an opposite direction , since the pool between him and Sam be too wide for even his lively leg .
Sam waddle off to the brook in the lane to rinse the mud from his nether man before face his mother , and be just wring himself out when Ben come up , breathless but good natured , for he felt that he have make an excellent bargain for himself and friend .

Sam forget his manner , but he remember his promise , and keep it so well that all the school wonder .
No one could guess the secret of Ben 's power over him , though it be evident that he have gain it in some sudden way , for at the least sign of Sam 's former trick Ben would crook his little finger and wag it warningly , or call out `` Bulrushes ! ''
and Sam subside with reluctant submission , to the great amazement of his mate .
When ask what it mean , Sa , turn sulky ; but Ben have much fun out of it , assure the other boy that those be the sign and password of a secret society to which he and Sam belong , and promise to tell them all about it if Sam would give him leave , which , of course , he would not .
This mystery , and the vain endeavor to find it out cause a lull in the war of the wood-pile , and before any new game be invent something happen which give the child plenty to talk about for a time .
A week after the secret alliance be form , Ben run in one evening with a letter for Miss Celia .

he have come !

ask Bab , prick up her car at once .

CHAPTER XXIII SOMEBODY COMES Bab and Betty have be play in the avenue all the afternoon several week later , but a the shadow begin to lengthen both agree to sit upon the gate and rest while wait for Ben , who have go nut with a party of boy .
When they play house Bab be always the father , and go hunt or fishing with great energy and success , bring home all sort of game , from elephant and crocodile to humming-birds and minnow .
Betty be the mother , and a most notable little housewife , always mix up imaginary delicacy with sand and dirt in old pan and broken china , which she bake in an oven of her own construction .
Both have work hard that day , and be glad to retire to their favorite lounging-place , where Bab be happy try to walk across the wide top bar without fall off , and Betty enjoy slow , luxurious swing while her sister be recover from her tumble .
On this occasion , have indulge their respective taste , they pause for a brief interval of conversation , sit side by side on the gate like a pair of plump gray chickens go to roost .

It be not a long story , but a very interesting one to this circle of listener ; all about the wild life on the plain trading for mustang , the terrible kick from a vicious horse that nearly kill Ben , sen. , the long month of unconsciousness in the California hospital , the slow recovery , the journey back , Mr. Smithers 's tale of the boy 's disappearance , and then the anxious trip to find out from Squire Allen where he now be .
`` I ask the hospital folk to write and tell you as soon a I know whether I be on my head or my heel , and they promise ; but they do n't ; so I come off the minute I could , and work my way back , expect to find you at the old place .

add , more quietly , `` What be you go to do now ?

`` Yes .

I may , for Mr. Barry do n't think he 'll want to rent it much longer , and some new arrangement will have to be make . ''

Anne , for her own good , must be tone down a trifle .
But it be a happy and beautiful bride who come down the old , homespun-carpeted stair that September noon -- the first bride of Green Gables , slender and shining-eyed , in the mist of her maiden veil , with her arm full of rose .
Gilbert , wait for her in the hall below , look up at her with adoring eye .
She be his at last , this evasive , long-sought Anne , win after year of patient waiting .
It be to him she be come in the sweet surrender of the bride .
Was he worthy of her ?
Could he make her as happy a he hop ?
If he fail her -- if he could not measure up to her standard of manhood -- then , a she hold out her hand , their eye meet and all doubt be sweep away in a glad certainty .
They belong to each other ; and , no matter what life might hold for them , it could never alter that .
Their happiness be in each other 's keep and both be unafraid .
They be marry in the sunshine of the old orchard , circle by the loving and kindly face of long-familiar friend .
Mr. Allan marry them , and the Reverend Jo make what Mrs. Rachel Lynde afterwards pronounce to be the `` most beautiful wedding prayer '' she have ever hear .
Birds do not often sing in September , but one sang sweetly from some hidden bough while Gilbert and Anne repeat their deathless vow .
Anne hear it and thrill to it ; Gilbert hear it , and wonder only that all the bird in the world have not burst into jubilant song ; Paul hear it and later write a lyric about it which be one of the most admired in his first volume of verse ; Charlotta the Fourth hear it and be blissfully sure it mean good luck for her adored Miss Shirley .
The bird sang until the ceremony be end and then it wind up with one mad little , glad little trill .
Never have the old gray-green house among it enfolding orchard know a blither , merry afternoon .
All the old jest and quip that must have do duty at wedding since Eden be serve up , and seem a new and brilliant and mirth-provoking a if they have never be utter before .
Laughter and joy have their way ; and when Anne and Gilbert leave to catch the Carmody train , with Paul a driver , the twin be ready with rice and old shoe , in the throwing of which Charlotta the Fourth and Mr. Harrison bore a valiant part .
Marilla stand at the gate and watch the carriage out of sight down the long lane with it bank of goldenrod .
Anne turn at it end to wave her last good-bye .
She be go -- Green Gables be her home no more ; Marilla 's face look very gray and old a she turn to the house which Anne have fill for fourteen year , and even in her absence , with light and life .
But Diana and her small fry , the Echo Lodge people and the Allans , have stay to help the two old lady over the loneliness of the first evening ; and they contrive to have a quietly pleasant little supper time , sit long around the table and chat over all the detail of the day .
While they be sit there Anne and Gilbert be alight from the train at Glen St. Mary .
CHAPTER 5 THE HOME COMING Dr. David Blythe have send his horse and buggy to meet them , and the urchin who have bring it slip away with a sympathetic grin , leave them to the delight of drive alone to their new home through the radiant evening .

Her new home could not yet be see ; but before her lay Four Winds Harbor like a great , shin mirror of rise and silver .
Far down , she saw it entrance between the bar of sand dune on one side and a steep , high , grim , red sandstone cliff on the other .
Beyond the bar the sea , calm and austere , dream in the afterlight .
The little fishing village , nestle in the cove where the sand-dunes meet the harbor shore , look like a great opal in the haze .
The sky over them be like a jewelled cup from which the dusk be pour ; the air be crisp with the compel tang of the sea , and the whole landscape be infuse with the subtlety of a sea evening .
A few dim sail drift along the darkening , fir-clad harbor shore .
A bell be ring from the tower of a little white church on the far side ; mellowly and dreamily sweet , the chime float across the water blent with the moan of the sea .

Far out along the horizon be the crinkled gray ribbon of a passing steamer 's smoke .
`` Oh , beautiful , beautiful , '' murmur Anne .

The girl be tall and wear a dress of pale blue print .

But it be the girl 's beauty which make Anne give a little gasp -- a beauty so mark that it must have attract attention anywhere .

ask Anne , in a low voice .

`` She be stand by that gate -- no , do n't look back .
She be still watch u .
I never saw such a beautiful face . ''
`` I do n't remember see any very handsome girl while I be here .

`` This girl be .
You ca n't have see her , or you would remember her .
Nobody could forget her .
I never saw such a face except in picture .
And her hair !
It make me think of Browning 's ` cord of gold ' and ` gorgeous snake ' ! ''
`` Probably she 's some visitor in Four Winds -- likely some one from that big summer hotel over the harbor . ''
`` She wear a white apron and she be drive geese . ''
`` She might do that for amusement .
Look , Anne -- there 's our house . ''

The first glimpse of her new home be a delight to eye and spirit -- it look so like a big , creamy seashell strand on the harbor shore .

`` Welcome home , '' he whisper , and hand in hand they step over the threshold of their house of dream .
CHAPTER 6 CAPTAIN JIM `` Old Doctor Dave '' and `` Mrs . Doctor Dave '' have come down to the little house to greet the bride and groom .

He understand it as well a I do .

`` No . ''

Come to think it over , I sorter remember that the dog look hungry . ''

CHAPTER 7 THE SCHOOLMASTER 'S BRIDE `` Who be the first bride who come to this house , Captain Jim ? ''
Anne ask , a they sit around the fireplace after supper .

ask Gilbert .

say I. '' ` She sail on the Royal William , the 20th of June , ' say he , ` and so she should be here by mid-July .

I know before I open it that it have good news for me .
I saw her a few night ago . '

But we wo n't talk of this again .
You wo n't be so much my friend if you think much about it . '
`` I tell him nothing could make me any less his friend .
But he jest shake his head and say , say he : '' ` Lad , I know .

I do n't blame them .

And we mortals all shrink from too close contact with God or devil . '

I remember them a if 't be yesterday , though I do n't know jest what he mean .
