Everybody have give up hope -- the Royal William be eight week overdue .
It be the middle of September and the schoolmaster 's bride have n't come -- never would come , we think .
`` There be a big storm then that last three day , and on the evening after it die away I go to the shore .
I find the schoolmaster there , lean with his arm fold against a big rock , gaze out to sea .
`` I speak to him but he do n't answer .
His eye seem to be look at something I could n't see .
His face be set , like a dead man 's . ''
` John -- John , ' I call out -- jest like that -- jest like a frightened child , ` wake up -- wake up . '
`` That strange , awful look seem to sorter fade out of his eye .
`` He turn his head and look at me .
I 've never forget his face -- never will forget it till I ship for my last voyage . ''
` All be well , lad , ' he say .
` I 've see the Royal William come around East Point .
She will be here by dawn .
Tomorrow night I shall sit with my bride by my own hearth-fire . '
`` Do you think he do see it ? ''
demand Captain Jim abruptly .
`` God know , '' say Gilbert softly .
`` Great love and great pain might compass we know not what marvel . ''
`` I be sure he do see it , '' say Anne earnestly .
`` Fol-de-rol , '' say Doctor Dave , but he speak with less conviction than usual .
`` Because , you know , '' say Captain Jim solemnly , `` the Royal William come into Four Winds Harbor at daylight the next morning .
`` Every soul in the Glen and along the shore be at the old wharf to meet her .
The schoolmaster have be watch there all night .
How we cheer a she sail up the channel . ''
Captain Jim 's eye be shin .
They be look at the Four Winds Harbor of sixty year agone , with a battered old ship sail through the sunrise splendor .
`` And Persis Leigh be on board ? ''
ask Anne .
`` Yes -- her and the captain 's wife .
They 'd have an awful passage -- storm after storm -- and their provision give out , too .
But there they be at last .
When Persis Leigh step onto the old wharf John Selwyn take her in his arm -- and folk stop cheer and begin to cry .
I cry myself , though 't be year , mind you , afore I 'd admit it .
Ai n't it funny how ashamed boy be of tear ? ''
`` Was Persis Leigh beautiful ? ''
ask Anne .
`` Well , I do n't know that you 'd call her beautiful exactly -- I -- do n't -- know , '' say Captain Jim slowly .
`` Somehow , you never get so far along a to wonder if she be handsome or not .
It jest do n't matter .
There be something so sweet and winsome about her that you have to love her , that be all .
But she be pleasant to look at -- big , clear , hazel eye and heap of glossy brown hair , and an English skin .
John and her be marry at our house that night at early candle-lighting ; everybody from far and near be there to see it and we all bring them down here afterwards .
Mistress Selwyn light the fire , and we go away and leave them sit here , jest a John have see in that vision of his .
A strange thing -- a strange thing !
But I 've see a turrible lot of strange thing in my time . ''
Captain Jim shake his head sagely .
`` It 's a dear story , '' say Anne , feel that for once she have get enough romance to satisfy her .
`` How long do they live here ? ''
`` Fifteen year .
I run off to sea soon after they be marry , like the young scalawag I be .
But every time I come back from a voyage I 'd head for here , even before I go home , and tell Mistress Selwyn all about it .
Fifteen happy year !
They have a sort of talent for happiness , them two .
Some folk be like that , if you 've notice .
They COULD N'T be unhappy for long , no matter what happen .
They quarrel once or twice , for they be both high-sperrited .
But Mistress Selwyn say to me once , say she , laugh in that pretty way of hers , ' I felt dreadful when John and I quarrel , but underneath it all I be very happy because I have such a nice husband to quarrel with and make it up with . '
Then they move to Charlottetown , and Ned Russell buy this house and bring his bride here .
They be a gay young pair , a I remember them .
Miss Elizabeth Russell be Alec 's sister .
She come to live with them a year or so later , and she be a creature of mirth , too .
The wall of this house must be sorter SOAKED with laughing and good time .
You 're the third bride I 've see come here , Mistress Blythe -- and the handsomest . ''
Captain Jim contrive to give his sunflower compliment the delicacy of a violet , and Anne wear it proudly .
She be look her best that night , with the bridal rise on her cheek and the love-light in her eye ; even gruff old Doctor Dave give her an approving glance , and tell his wife , a they drive home together , that that red-headed wife of the boy 's be something of a beauty .
`` I must be get back to the light , '' announce Captain Jim .
`` I 've enj ` yed this evening something tremenjus . ''
`` You must come often to see u , '' say Anne .
`` I wonder if you 'd give that invitation if you know how likely I 'll be to accept it , '' Captain Jim remark whimsically .
`` Which be another way of say you wonder if I mean it , '' smile Anne .
`` I do , ` cross my heart , ' a we use to say at school . ''
`` Then I 'll come .
You 're likely to be pester with me at any hour .
And I 'll be proud to have you drop down and visit me now and then , too .
Gin ` rally I have n't anyone to talk to but the First Mate , bless his sociable heart .
He 's a mighty good listener , and have forget more 'n any MacAllister of them all ever know , but he be n't much of a conversationalist .
You 're young and I 'm old , but our soul be about the same age , I reckon .
We both belong to the race that know Joseph , a Cornelia Bryant would say . ''
`` The race that know Joseph ? ''
puzzle Anne .
`` Yes .
Cornelia divide all the folk in the world into two kind -- the race that know Joseph and the race that do n't .
If a person sorter see eye to eye with you , and have pretty much the same idea about thing , and the same taste in joke -- why , then he belong to the race that know Joseph . ''
`` Oh , I understand , '' exclaim Anne , light break in upon her .
`` It 's what I use to call -- and still call in quotation mark ` kindred spirit . ' ''
`` Jest so -- jest so , '' agree Captain Jim .
`` We 're it , whatever IT be .
When you come in tonight , Mistress Blythe , I say to myself , say I , ` Yes , she 's of the race that know Joseph . '
And mighty glad I be , for if it be n't so we could n't have have any real satisfaction in each other 's company .
The race that know Joseph be the salt of the airth , I reckon . ''
The moon have just rise when Anne and Gilbert go to the door with their guest .
Four Winds Harbor be begin to be a thing of dream and glamour and enchantment -- a spellbound haven where no tempest might ever ravin .
The Lombardies down the lane , tall and sombre a the priestly form of some mystic band , be tip with silver .
`` Always like Lombardies , '' say Captain Jim , wave a long arm at them .
`` They 're the tree of princess .
They 're out of fashion now .
Folks complain that they die at the top and get ragged-looking .
So they do -- so they do , if you do n't risk your neck every spring climb up a light ladder to trim them out .
I always do it for Miss Elizabeth , so her Lombardies never get out-at-elbows .
She be especially fond of them .
She like their dignity and stand-offishness .
THEY do n't hobnob with every Tom , Dick and Harry .
If it 's maple for company , Mistress Blythe , it 's Lombardies for society . ''
`` What a beautiful night , '' say Mrs . Doctor Dave , a she climb into the Doctor 's buggy .
`` Most night be beautiful , '' say Captain Jim .
`` But I ` low that moonlight over Four Winds make me sorter wonder what 's leave for heaven .
The moon 's a great friend of mine , Mistress Blythe .
I 've love her ever since I can remember .
When I be a little chap of eight I fell asleep in the garden one evening and be n't miss .
I wake up along in the night and I be most scared to death .
What shadow and queer noise there be !
I durs n't move .
Jest crouch there quake , poor small mite .
Seemed 's if there be n't anyone in the world but meself and it be mighty big .
Then all at once I saw the moon look down at me through the apple bough , jest like an old friend .
I be comfort right off .
Got up and walk to the house as brave a a lion , look at her .
Many 's the night I 've watch her from the deck of my vessel , on sea far away from here .
Why do n't you folks tell me to take in the slack of my jaw and go home ? ''
The laughter of the goodnights die away .
Anne and Gilbert walk hand in hand around their garden .
The brook that run across the corner dimple pellucidly in the shadow of the birch .
The poppy along it bank be like shallow cup of moonlight .
Flowers that have be plant by the hand of the schoolmaster 's bride fling their sweetness on the shadowy air , like the beauty and blessing of sacred yesterday .
Anne pause in the gloom to gather a spray .
`` I love to smell flower in the dark , '' she say .
`` You get hold of their soul then .
Oh , Gilbert , this little house be all I 've dream it .
And I 'm so glad that we be not the first who have keep bridal tryst here ! ''
CHAPTER 8 MISS CORNELIA BRYANT COMES TO CALL That September be a month of golden mist and purple haze at Four Winds Harbor -- a month of sun-steeped day and of night that be swim in moonlight , or pulsate with star .
No storm mar it , no rough wind blew .
Anne and Gilbert put their nest in order , ramble on the shore , sail on the harbor , drive about Four Winds and the Glen , or through the ferny , sequester road of the wood around the harbor head ; in short , have such a honeymoon a any lover in the world might have envy them .
`` If life be to stop short just now it would still have be richly worth while , just for the sake of these past four week , would n't it ? ''
say Anne .
`` I do n't suppose we will ever have four such perfect week again -- but we 've HAD them .
Everything -- wind , weather , folk , house of dream -- have conspire to make our honeymoon delightful .
There have n't even be a rainy day since we come here . ''
`` And we have n't quarrel once , '' tease Gilbert .
`` Well , ` that 's a pleasure all the great for be defer , ' '' quote Anne .
`` I 'm so glad we decide to spend our honeymoon here .
Our memory of it will always belong here , in our house of dream , instead of be scatter about in strange place . ''
There be a certain tang of romance and adventure in the atmosphere of their new home which Anne have never find in Avonlea .
There , although she have live in sight of the sea , it have not enter intimately into her life .
In Four Winds it surround her and call to her constantly .
From every window of her new home she saw some vary aspect of it .
Its haunting murmur be ever in her ear .
Vessels sail up the harbor every day to the wharf at the Glen , or sail out again through the sunset , bound for port that might be half way round the globe .
Fishing boat go white-winged down the channel in the morning , and return laden in the evening .
Sailors and fisher-folk travel the red , wind harbor road , light-hearted and content .
There be always a certain sense of thing go to happen -- of adventure and farings-forth .
The way of Four Winds be less staid and settle and groove than those of Avonlea ; wind of change blew over them ; the sea call ever to the dweller on shore , and even those who might not answer it call felt the thrill and unrest and mystery and possibility of it .
`` I understand now why some men must go to sea , '' say Anne .
`` That desire which come to u all at time -- ` to sail beyond the bourne of sunset ' -- must be very imperious when it be bear in you .
I do n't wonder Captain Jim run away because of it .
I never see a ship sail out of the channel , or a gull soaring over the sand-bar , without wish I be on board the ship or have wing , not like a dove ` to fly away and be at rest , ' but like a gull , to sweep out into the very heart of a storm . ''
`` You 'll stay right here with me , Anne-girl , '' say Gilbert lazily .
`` I wo n't have you fly away from me into the heart of storm . ''
They be sit on their red sand-stone doorstep in the late afternoon .
Great tranquillity be all about them in land and sea and sky .
Silvery gull be soar over them .
The horizon be lace with long trail of frail , pinkish cloud .
The hushed air be thread with a murmurous refrain of minstrel wind and wave .
Pale aster be blow in the sere and misty meadow between them and the harbor .
`` Doctors who have to be up all night wait on sick folk do n't feel very adventurous , I suppose , '' Anne say indulgently .
`` If you have have a good sleep last night , Gilbert , you 'd be as ready a I be for a flight of imagination . ''
`` I do good work last night , Anne , '' say Gilbert quietly .
`` Under God , I save a life .
This be the first time I could ever really claim that .
In other case I may have help ; but , Anne , if I have not stay at Allonby 's last night and fought death hand to hand , that woman would have die before morning .
I try an experiment that be certainly never try in Four Winds before .
I doubt if it be ever try anywhere before outside of a hospital .
It be a new thing in Kingsport hospital last winter .
I could never have dare try it here if I have not be absolutely certain that there be no other chance .
I risk it -- and it succeed .
As a result , a good wife and mother be save for long year of happiness and usefulness .
As I drive home this morning , while the sun be rise over the harbor , I thank God that I have choose the profession I do .
I have fight a good fight and win -- think of it , Anne , WON , against the Great Destroyer .
It 's what I dream of do long ago when we talk together of what we want to do in life .
That dream of mine come true this morning . ''
`` Was that the only one of your dream that have come true ? ''
ask Anne , who know perfectly well what the substance of his answer would be , but want to hear it again .
`` YOU know , Anne-girl , '' say Gilbert , smile into her eye .
At that moment there be certainly two perfectly happy people sit on the doorstep of a little white house on the Four Winds Harbor shore .
Presently Gilbert say , with a change of tone , `` Do I or do I not see a full-rigged ship sail up our lane ? ''
Anne look and spring up .
`` That must be either Miss Cornelia Bryant or Mrs. Moore come to call , '' she say .
`` I 'm go into the office , and if it be Miss Cornelia I warn you that I 'll eavesdrop , '' say Gilbert .
`` From all I 've hear regard Miss Cornelia I conclude that her conversation will not be dull , to say the least . ''
`` It may be Mrs. Moore . ''
`` I do n't think Mrs. Moore be build on those line .
I saw her work in her garden the other day , and , though I be too far away to see clearly , I think she be rather slender .
She do n't seem very socially inclined when she have never call on you yet , although she 's your near neighbor . ''
`` She ca n't be like Mrs. Lynde , after all , or curiosity would have bring her , '' say Anne .
`` This caller be , I think , Miss Cornelia . ''
Miss Cornelia it be ; moreover , Miss Cornelia have not come to make any brief and fashionable wedding call .
She have her work under her arm in a substantial parcel , and when Anne ask her to stay she promptly take off her capacious sun-hat , which have be hold on her head , despite irreverent September breeze , by a tight elastic band under her hard little knob of fair hair .
No hat pin for Miss Cornelia , an it please ye !
Elastic band have be good enough for her mother and they be good enough for HER .
She have a fresh , round , pink-and-white face , and jolly brown eye .
She do not look in the least like the traditional old maid , and there be something in her expression which win Anne instantly .
With her old instinctive quickness to discern kindred spirit she know she be go to like Miss Cornelia , in spite of uncertain oddity of opinion , and certain oddity of attire .
Nobody but Miss Cornelia would have come to make a call array in a striped blue-and-white apron and a wrapper of chocolate print , with a design of huge , pink rose scatter over it .
And nobody but Miss Cornelia could have look dignified and suitably garb in it .
Had Miss Cornelia be enter a palace to call on a prince 's bride , she would have be just a dignified and just a wholly mistress of the situation .
She would have trail her rose-spattered flounce over the marble floor just a unconcernedly , and she would have proceed just a calmly to disabuse the mind of the princess of any idea that the possession of a mere man , be he prince or peasant , be anything to brag of .
`` I 've bring my work , Mrs. Blythe , dearie , '' she remark , unroll some dainty material .
`` I 'm in a hurry to get this do , and there be n't any time to lose . ''
Anne look in some surprise at the white garment spread over Miss Cornelia 's ample lap .
It be certainly a baby 's dress , and it be most beautifully make , with tiny frill and tuck .
Miss Cornelia adjust her glass and fell to embroider with exquisite stitch .
`` This be for Mrs. Fred Proctor up at the Glen , '' she announce .
`` She 's expect her eighth baby any day now , and not a stitch have she ready for it .
The other seven have wear out all she make for the first , and she 's never have time or strength or spirit to make any more .
That woman be a martyr , Mrs. Blythe , believe ME .
When she marry Fred Proctor I know how it would turn out .
He be one of your wicked , fascinate men .
After he get married he leave off be fascinating and just keep on be wicked .
He drink and he neglect his family .
Is n't that like a man ?
I do n't know how Mrs. Proctor would ever keep her child decently clothe if her neighbor do n't help her out . ''
As Anne be afterwards to learn , Miss Cornelia be the only neighbor who trouble herself much about the decency of the young Proctors .
`` When I hear this eighth baby be come I decide to make some thing for it , '' Miss Cornelia go on .
`` This be the last and I want to finish it today . ''
`` It 's certainly very pretty , '' say Anne .
`` I 'll get my sewing and we 'll have a little thimble party of two .
You be a beautiful sewer , Miss Bryant . ''
`` Yes , I 'm the best sewer in these part , '' say Miss Cornelia in a matter-of-fact tone .
`` I ought to be !
Lord , I 've do more of it than if I 'd have a hundred child of my own , believe ME !
I s ` pose I 'm a fool , to be put hand embroidery on this dress for an eighth baby .
But , Lord , Mrs. Blythe , dearie , it be n't to blame for be the eighth , and I kind of wish it to have one real pretty dress , just a if it WAS want .
Nobody 's want the poor mite -- so I put some extra fuss on it little thing just on that account . ''
`` Any baby might be proud of that dress , '' say Anne , feel still more strongly that she be go to like Miss Cornelia .
`` I s ` pose you 've be think I be never come to call on you , '' resume Miss Cornelia .
`` But this be harvest month , you know , and I 've be busy -- and a lot of extra hand hang round , eat more 'n they work , just like the men .
I 'd have come yesterday , but I go to Mrs. Roderick MacAllister 's funeral .
At first I think my head be ache so badly I could n't enjoy myself if I do go .
But she be a hundred year old , and I 'd always promise myself that I 'd go to her funeral . ''
`` Was it a successful function ? ''
ask Anne , notice that the office door be ajar .
`` What 's that ?
Oh , yes , it be a tremendous funeral .
She have a very large connection .
There be over one hundred and twenty carriage in the procession .
There be one or two funny thing happen .
I think that die I would to see old Joe Bradshaw , who be an infidel and never darken the door of a church , sing ` Safe in the Arms of Jesus ' with great gusto and fervor .
He glory in sing -- that 's why he never miss a funeral .
Poor Mrs. Bradshaw do n't look much like sing -- all wear out slaving .
Old Joe start out once in a while to buy her a present and bring home some new kind of farm machinery .
Is n't that like a man ?
But what else would you expect of a man who never go to church , even a Methodist one ?
I be real thankful to see you and the young Doctor in the Presbyterian church your first Sunday .
No doctor for me who be n't a Presbyterian . ''
`` We be in the Methodist church last Sunday evening , '' say Anne wickedly .
`` Oh , I s ` pose Dr. Blythe have to go to the Methodist church once in a while or he would n't get the Methodist practice . ''
`` We like the sermon very much , '' declare Anne boldly .
`` And I think the Methodist minster 's prayer be one of the most beautiful I ever hear . ''
`` Oh , I 've no doubt he can pray .
I never hear anyone make more beautiful prayer than old Simon Bentley , who be always drunk , or hop to be , and the drunker he be the good he pray . ''
`` The Methodist minister be very fine look , '' say Anne , for the benefit of the office door .
`` Yes , he 's quite ornamental , '' agree Miss Cornelia .
`` Oh , and VERY ladylike .
And he think that every girl who look at him fall in love with him -- a if a Methodist minister , wander about like any Jew , be such a prize !
If you and the young doctor take MY advice , you wo n't have much to do with the Methodists .
My motto be -- if you ARE a Presbyterian , BE a Presbyterian . ''
`` Do n't you think that Methodists go to heaven as well a Presbyterians ? ''
ask Anne smilelessly .
`` That be n't for US to decide .
It 's in high hand than ours , '' say Miss Cornelia solemnly .
`` But I ai n't go to associate with them on earth whatever I may have to do in heaven .
THIS Methodist minister be n't marry .
The last one they have be , and his wife be the silly , flighty little thing I ever saw .
I tell her husband once that he should have wait till she be grow up before he marry her .
He say he want to have the training of her .
Was n't that like a man ? ''
`` It 's rather hard to decide just when people ARE grow up , '' laugh Anne .
`` That 's a true word , dearie .
Some be grow up when they 're bear , and others ai n't grow up when they 're eighty , believe ME .
That same Mrs. Roderick I be speak of never grow up .
She be a foolish when she be a hundred a when she be ten . ''
`` Perhaps that be why she live so long , '' suggest Anne .
`` Maybe 't be .
I 'd rather live fifty sensible year than a hundred foolish one . ''
`` But just think what a dull world it would be if everyone be sensible , '' plead Anne .
Miss Cornelia disdain any skirmish of flippant epigram .
`` Mrs. Roderick be a Milgrave , and the Milgraves never have much sense .
Her nephew , Ebenezer Milgrave , use to be insane for year .
He believe he be dead and use to rage at his wife because she would n't bury him .
I 'd a-done it . ''
Miss Cornelia look so grimly determine that Anne could almost see her with a spade in her hand .
`` Do n't you know ANY good husband , Miss Bryant ? ''
`` Oh , yes , lot of them -- over yonder , '' say Miss Cornelia , wave her hand through the open window towards the little graveyard of the church across the harbor .
`` But living -- go about in the flesh ? ''
persist Anne .
`` Oh , there 's a few , just to show that with God all thing be possible , '' acknowledge Miss Cornelia reluctantly .
`` I do n't deny that an odd man here and there , if he 's caught young and train up proper , and if his mother have spank him well beforehand , may turn out a decent be .
YOUR husband , now , be n't so bad , a men go , from all I hear .
I s ` pose '' -- Miss Cornelia look sharply at Anne over her glass -- `` you think there 's nobody like him in the world . ''
`` There be n't , '' say Anne promptly .
`` Ah , well , I hear another bride say that once , '' sigh Miss Cornelia .
`` Jennie Dean think when she marry that there be n't anybody like HER husband in the world .
And she be right -- there be n't !
And a good thing , too , believe ME !
He lead her an awful life -- and he be court his second wife while Jennie be die .
`` Was n't that like a man ?
However , I hope YOUR confidence will be well justify , dearie .
The young doctor be take real well .
I be afraid at first he might n't , for folk hereabouts have always think old Doctor Dave the only doctor in the world .
Doctor Dave have n't much tact , to be sure -- he be always talk of rope in house where someone have hang himself .
But folk forget their hurt feeling when they have a pain in their stomach .
If he 'd be a minister instead of a doctor they 'd never have forgive him .
Soul-ache do n't worry folks near as much a stomach-ache .
Seeing a we 're both Presbyterians and no Methodists around , will you tell me your candid opinion of OUR minister ? ''
`` Why -- really -- I -- well , '' hesitate Anne .
Miss Cornelia nod .
`` Exactly .
I agree with you , dearie .
We make a mistake when we call HIM .
His face just look like one of those long , narrow stone in the graveyard , do n't it ?
` Sacred to the memory ' ought to be write on his forehead .
I shall never forget the first sermon he preach after he come .
It be on the subject of everyone do what they be best fit for -- a very good subject , of course ; but such illustration a he use !
He say , ` If you have a cow and an apple tree , and if you tie the apple tree in your stable and plant the cow in your orchard , with her leg up , how much milk would you get from the apple tree , or how many apple from the cow ? '
Did you ever hear the like in your born day , dearie ?
I be so thankful there be no Methodists there that day -- they 'd never have be do hoot over it .
But what I dislike most in him be his habit of agree with everybody , no matter what be say .
If you say to him , ` You 're a scoundrel , ' he 'd say , with that smooth smile of his , ` Yes , that 's so . '
A minister should have more backbone .
The long and the short of it be , I consider him a reverend jackass .
But , of course , this be just between you and me .
When there be Methodists in hear I praise him to the sky .
Some folk think his wife dress too gay , but I say when she have to live with a face like that she need something to cheer her up .
You 'll never hear ME condemn a woman for her dress .
I 'm only too thankful when her husband be n't too mean and miserly to allow it .
Not that I bother much with dress myself .
Women just dress to please the men , and I 'd never stoop to THAT .
I have have a real placid , comfortable life , dearie , and it 's just because I never care a cent what the men think . ''
`` Why do you hate the men so , Miss Bryant ? ''
`` Lord , dearie , I do n't hate them .
They be n't worth it .
I just sort of despise them .
I think I 'll like YOUR husband if he keep on a he have begin .
But apart from him about the only men in the world I 've much use for be the old doctor and Captain Jim . ''
`` Captain Jim be certainly splendid , '' agree Anne cordially .
`` Captain Jim be a good man , but he 's kind of vex in one way .
You CA N'T make him mad .
I 've try for twenty year and he just keep on be placid .
It do sort of rile me .
And I s ` pose the woman he should have marry get a man who go into tantrum twice a day . ''
`` Who be she ? ''
`` Oh , I do n't know , dearie .
I never remember of Captain Jim make up to anybody .
He be edge on old as far a my memory go .
He 's seventy-six , you know .
I never hear any reason for his stay a bachelor , but there must be one , believe ME .
He sail all his life till five year ago , and there 's no corner of the earth he have n't poke his nose into .
He and Elizabeth Russell be great crony , all their life , but they never have any notion of sweet-hearting .
Elizabeth never marry , though she have plenty of chance .
She be a great beauty when she be young .
The year the Prince of Wales come to the Island she be visit her uncle in Charlottetown and he be a Government official , and so she get invite to the great ball .
She be the pretty girl there , and the Prince dance with her , and all the other woman he do n't dance with be furious about it , because their social standing be high than hers and they say he should n't have pass them over .
Elizabeth be always very proud of that dance .
Mean folk say that be why she never marry -- she could n't put up with an ordinary man after dance with a prince .
But that be n't so .
She tell me the reason once -- it be because she have such a temper that she be afraid she could n't live peaceably with any man .
She HAD an awful temper -- she use to have to go upstairs and bite piece out of her bureau to keep it down by time .
But I tell her that be n't any reason for not marry if she want to .
There 's no reason why we should let the men have a monopoly of temper , be there , Mrs. Blythe , dearie ? ''
`` I 've a bit of temper myself , '' sigh Anne .
`` It 's well you have , dearie .
You wo n't be half so likely to be tread on , believe ME !
My , how that golden glow of yours be bloom !
Your garden look fine .
Poor Elizabeth always take such care of it . ''
`` I love it , '' say Anne .
